     1                  S T I P U L A T I O N

     2

     3          It is stipulated and agreed by and between

     4  Counsel that the testimony of the witness, RICHARD

     5  HALPRIN, is hereby being taken pursuant to Notice

     6  under the Louisiana Code of Civil Procedure for all

     7  purposes permitted under law.

     8

     9          The witness reserves the right to read and

    10  sign the deposition.  The original is to be

    11  delivered to and retained by RYAN CAUGHEY, ESQ., for

    12  proper filing with the Clerk of Court.

    13

    14          All objections, except those as to the form

    15  of the questions and/or responsiveness of the

    16  answers, are reserved until the time of the trial of

    17  this cause.

     1              having been first duly sworn, was

     2              examined and testified as follows:

     3

     4   EXAMINATION

     5   BY MR. CAUGHEY:

     6        Q.    Good morning, sir.  My name is Ryan

     7   Caughey and we met a few minutes ago.  I represent

     8   the Westlake Defendants in this case.  I'm in from

     9   Houston.  It's good to meet you.

    10        A.    Nice to meet you.

    11        Q.    What is your name, sir?

    12        A.    Richard Halprin, Rick Halprin.

    13        Q.    What is your address?

    14        A.    9757 Lemonwood Terrace, Boynton Beach,

    15   Florida, 33437.

    16        Q.    And that's your permanent address?

    17        A.    That is my permanent address.

    18        Q.    So you flew in to give testimony today?

    19        A.    I did.

    20        Q.    Have you given a deposition before, sir?

    21        A.    One time.

    22        Q.    When was that?

    23        A.    Twenty-five years ago potentially.  It

    24   was probably in the early 2000's.

    25        Q.    Do you recall what the general subject


                                                          14


     1   matter was of the lawsuit?

     2        A.    Absolutely.

     3        Q.    What was it?

     4        A.    It was a dispute between volumes of oil

     5   -- oil barrels being paid to one of the companies I

     6   used to work for versus a major company.  And I used

     7   to do all the marketing for them when I retired from

     8   that company.  They called me back to testify.

     9        Q.    Was this when you were at Somerset?

    10        A.    I was at Somerset and I went back to do

    11   a deposition for W&T Offshore.

    12        Q.    And do you know whether W&T was the

    13   plaintiff or the defendant in that case?

    14        A.    They were the plaintiff.

    15        Q.    And could you describe to the best of

    16   your recollection what the claim W&T made in that

    17   case was?

    18        A.    That they were being underpaid for the

    19   volumes that they were producing.

    20        Q.    Do you recall who the defendant was in

    21   that case?

    22        A.    Chevron.

    23        Q.    Have you ever testified at a trial?

    24        A.    No -- no, yes, I have one time.

    25        Q.    When was that?


                                                          15


     1        A.    1980's, late 80's potentially.

     2        Q.    Do you recall what that trial was about?

     3        A.    I was an expert witness on accounting

     4   software in the oil and gas business.

     5        Q.    Do you recall who the parties were in

     6   that case?

     7        A.    Uhmm.  I want to say -- I don't recall.

     8   I know one of them was Warren Seal.  And I don't

     9   know if he was the defendant or the plaintiff.  It's

    10   been a while.

    11        Q.    Do you recall the general nature of what

    12   opinions you offered as an expert witness in that

    13   case?

    14        A.    Just how the software worked.  How the

    15   billings came out -- should have come out versus

    16   what the other party was using.

    17        Q.    Have you ever been retained as an expert

    18   witness in any other case?

    19        A.    No, sir.

    20        Q.    That's the only one?

    21        A.    Yes, sir.

    22        Q.    You do understand that you're sworn

    23   under oath and testifying under oath as if you were

    24   in a court of law today, correct?

    25        A.    I do.


                                                          16


     1        Q.    And I don't -- you've done this before,

     2   so not a lot of ground rules to go over.  The only

     3   thing for the benefit of Marybeth is if you could

     4   let me finish my question before you answer.  And

     5   I'll endeavor to let you finish your answer before I

     6   launch in.

     7              Does that work?

     8        A.    Yes, sir.

     9        Q.    All righty.

    10              You received a degree from the

    11   University of New Orleans; is that right?

    12        A.    That's correct.

    13        Q.    In accounting?

    14        A.    That is correct.

    15        Q.    When was that?

    16        A.    1980.

    17        Q.    Are you a CPA?

    18        A.    Unlicensed CPA.

    19        Q.    What do you mean "unlicensed"?

    20        A.    I don't maintain my license anymore. I

    21   was a licensed CPA at one point.

    22        Q.    Until when did you maintain your

    23   license?

    24        A.    I don't remember.

    25        Q.    Any approximation?


                                                          17


     1        A.    2010 maybe.  It's been a while.

     2        Q.    More than a decade?

     3        A.    More than 10 years.

     4        Q.    Do you have any other professional

     5   certifications?

     6        A.    No.

     7        Q.    You have --and we'll get into it, but

     8   you have for decades worked in the oil and gas

     9   industry, right?

    10        A.    Yes.

    11        Q.    You don't -- you have always done so in

    12   a financial or accounting or controlling capacity,

    13   right?

    14        A.    Yes.

    15        Q.    You are not any sort of petroleum

    16   engineer or geologist or expert in oil and gas

    17   drilling, right?

    18                 MR. MADIGAN:  Object to form.

    19                 Go ahead.

    20        A.    Absolutely not.  No, I'm not.

    21        Q.    Okay.

    22              Nor do you have any degrees in any of

    23   those subjects, right?

    24        A.    Correct.

    25        Q.    Other than your degree from the


                                                          18


     1   University of New Orleans, you don't have any other

     2   degrees, right?

     3        A.    Correct.

     4        Q.    Nor any other certifications other than

     5   the CPA license or former license?

     6        A.    Well, I did have a real estate license.

     7        Q.    Okay.

     8              Other than your CPA and your real estate

     9   license, any other licenses or certifications that

    10   you've received?

    11        A.    No, none.

    12        Q.    Okay.

    13              Could you briefly describe for me your

    14   professional career after leaving the University of

    15   New Orleans in 1980.  Just start me off.  What did

    16   you do after college?

    17        A.    After college I went right to Odeco.

    18        Q.    Can you spell that.

    19        A.    O-d-e-c-o.  Odeco was a subsidiary of

    20   Murphy Oil & Gas.

    21        Q.    What did you do for Odeco?

    22        A.    I was the property accountant initially.

    23        Q.    How long did you work for Odeco?

    24        A.    A little over five years.

    25        Q.    You left Odeco in mid-1980's.  What did


                                                          19


     1   you do next?

     2        A.    I went to Crescent Exploration.

     3        Q.    And what was your role at Crescent?

     4        A.    Assistant controller, handling some

     5   financial, mostly joint interest billings, analysis,

     6   performers potentially.

     7        Q.    What was Crescent's business?

     8        A.    Oil and gas.

     9        Q.    Exploration and production?

    10        A.    Yes.

    11        Q.    How long did you stay at Crescent?

    12        A.    Two years.

    13        Q.    What came next?

    14        A.    Graham Resources.

    15        Q.    Was that another oil and gas exploration

    16   production company?

    17        A.    They were -- they were a limited

    18   partnership involved in the oil and gas business.

    19        Q.    Were you based in New Orleans this whole

    20   time?

    21        A.    Yes.  I lived in Metairie.

    22        Q.    How long did you stay at Graham?

    23        A.    Two years.

    24        Q.    Okay.

    25              What came after that?


                                                          20


     1        A.    W&T Offshore.

     2        Q.    And you were at W&T all the way through

     3   about 1998, right?

     4        A.    1998 is correct.

     5        Q.    And you joined W&T in about 1990?

     6        A.    1990.

     7        Q.    What was W&T's business?

     8        A.    E&P, exploration and production.

     9        Q.    And were you still in New Orleans with

    10   W&T?

    11        A.    I was the whole time.

    12        Q.    And what --

    13        A.    In Metairie, I'm sorry.

    14        Q.    What was your position at W&T?

    15        A.    I was the accounting manager.

    16        Q.    Was that true the entire time that you

    17   were with the company?

    18        A.    Yes.

    19        Q.    In 1998 you joined Somerset Production

    20   Company, right?

    21        A.    That's correct.

    22        Q.    As its Chief Financial Officer?

    23        A.    That's correct.

    24        Q.    What was Somerset's business?

    25        A.    E&P.


                                                          21


     1        Q.    Okay.

     2              Still in New Orleans?

     3        A.    No.

     4        Q.    Okay.

     5        A.    Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania area, Indiana,

     6   Pennsylvania specifically.

     7        Q.    And you were at Somerset until

     8   approximately 2003; is that right?

     9        A.    '02 or '03, thereabouts.  Yeah, '03 --

    10   yeah, '03.  In that area.  And we sold our company.

    11        Q.    Who was Somerset sold to, do you recall?

    12        A.    It's a major here in Houston -- not

    13   major.  Uhmm.  Oh, yeah.  Uhmm.  EOG Resources.

    14        Q.    Right down the street from my office.

    15              What did you do after leaving Somerset

    16   or after Somerset was sold?

    17        A.    I -- we had success at Somerset.  So

     6                 MR. MADIGAN:  No, nothing from us.

     7                 THE WITNESS:  Thank you so much.

     8                 THE VIDEOGRAPHER:  This concludes the

     9              deposition and the time is 4:19 p.m.

    10                 THE COURT REPORTER:  Do you want the

    11              rough draft of this, Mr. Garner?

    12                 MR. GARNER:  I do, yes.

    13                 MR. CAUGHEY:  And so do we.

    14                 THE COURT REPORTER:  Amiee, do you

    15              want the rough draft?

    16                 MS. HEBERT:  If you're handing it out.

    17              I don't really need it, Marybeth.

    18                 THE COURT REPORTER:  Then I won't give

    19              it to you.  No worries.

    20

    21           (Deposition adjourned at 4:20 p.m.)
